ğŸ¬ **DiGiTaL DiVe Narrative Image Generation Framework**
1. **Cover Image (Scene Introduction)**
	â€¢	**Purpose:** Establish tone, mood, and symbolic entry point.
	â€¢	**Prompt Template:**
	â€¢	*Wide vertical 9:16 frame. A symbolic object or environment (e.g., glowing graffiti heart, broken throne, willow tree through asphalt). High-contrast lighting (neon vs dark). Typography organically embedded (graffiti, billboard, sign).*
	â€¢	**Transitions:** Begin with **slow aerial pan** or **fade-in from darkness**.

2. **Transition (Shift / Detail)**
	â€¢	**Purpose:** Bridge focus from macro to micro or shift mood.
	â€¢	**Prompt Template:**
	â€¢	*Close-up of symbolic lyric object (e.g., cracked cassette, dripping neon tear, barbed willow branch). Background blurred, softer lighting. Optional ghostly text integrated in mist, reflection, or scratched surface.*
	â€¢	**Transitions:** Use **slow zoom-in/out** or **blur-to-clear reveal**.

3. **Main Image (Core Action / Emotion)**
	â€¢	**Purpose:** Showcase the central action or emotional highlight.
	â€¢	**Prompt Template:**
	â€¢	*Dynamic vertical 9:16 scene. Character(s) in motion (singing, rebelling, breaking down). Dramatic neon lighting palette (deep blues, pinks, reds). Typography as glowing signage or wall graffiti (chorus lyric). Action foregrounded, environment contextual.*
	â€¢	**Transitions:** **Tracking shot or dolly sweep**, carry movement across cuts.

4. **Filler (Pause / Reflection)**
	â€¢	**Purpose:** Add atmosphere, give narrative breathing room.
	â€¢	**Prompt Template:**
	â€¢	*Static or slow tilt. Symbolic element (discarded item, rising smoke, graffiti wall). Warm or nostalgic lighting (golden, soft shadows). Typography faint or etched subtly (â€œhope never diesâ€).*
	â€¢	**Transitions:** **Slow fade into dawn light**, or **subtle upward camera tilt**.

5. **Next-Scene Transition**
	â€¢	**Purpose:** Expand scope or shift location for next narrative beat.
	â€¢	**Prompt Template:**
	â€¢	*Panoramic 16:9 or wide vertical 9:16 view. Wider environment revealed (alley to skyline, ruins to protest). Colors fade or shift (pastel dawn, muted blues). Typography optional as lingering echo.*
	â€¢	**Transitions:** **Whip-pan**, **glitch flicker**, or **crane pull-out**.

âš™ï¸ **Technical Defaults**
	â€¢	**Aspect Ratios:**
	â—¦	Characters â†’ 9:16 (1080x1920)
	â—¦	Cityscapes / Wide views â†’ 16:9 (1280x720)
	â—¦	Symbols / Objects â†’ 1:1 (1024x1024)
	â€¢	**Typography:** Embedded naturally in-world, never overlaid.
	â€¢	**Backgrounds:** Isolated + solid color for symbolic object focus.
	â€¢	**Lighting:** Consistently cinematic, neon-vs-dark contrasts, transitions softened.

ğŸ”„ **Batching Workflow**
	â€¢	Always **generate 4 images per batch**:
	â—¦	1 Ã— Cover or Main
	â—¦	1 Ã— Transition
	â—¦	1 Ã— Filler
	â—¦	1 Ã— Next-Scene (or additional Main)
	â€¢	After each batch: propose **4 new lyric-rooted expansions**:
	1	Expand on metaphor
	2	Explore secondary symbol
	3	Add emotional shift
	4	Alternate perspective

ğŸ§° Step 1. Install Miniforge (conda-forge native)
Miniforge is the lightweight conda distribution that defaults to the conda-forge channel.
Download Miniforge for macOS Intel

Run the installer
bash Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh
Then restart your shell so conda works.
ğŸ Step 2. Install Mamba
Mamba is a fast drop-in replacement for conda.
conda install mamba -n base -c conda-forge
Check it works:
mamba --version
ğŸ§© Step 3. Create a dedicated environment
Letâ€™s make an environment for storyboard generation and export scripting:
mamba create -n storyboard python=3.11 pandas numpy rich jinja2 typer
mamba activate storyboard
These packages give you:
pandas â€“ CSV/JSON handling
numpy â€“ quick array math
rich â€“ styled console output
jinja2 â€“ templating (for readme generation)
typer â€“ command-line interface scripting

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI
Command-line interface for generating, packaging, and exporting cinematic
storyboards (CSV + JSON + text) into a zipped deliverable.
"""
import json, pathlib, zipfile, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track
app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()
ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
DATA = ROOT / "data"
TEMPLATES = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"
def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    """Render the README file from the Jinja2 template."""
    template = Template(TEMPLATES.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)
def package_storyboard(title: str):
    """Zip all storyboard files and a generated README into one archive."""
    console.print(f"[bold cyan]Building storyboard package for {title}...[/]")




 



# Ensure data folder exists

if not DATA.exists():

 Â   console.print("[red]Data folder not found![/]")

 Â   raise typer.Exit(1)

â€‹

# Load JSON data to count scenes

json_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.json"

csv_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.csv"

txt_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.txt"

â€‹

if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():

 Â   console.print("[red]Missing storyboard data files![/]")

 Â   raise typer.Exit(1)

â€‹

with open(json_path) as f:

 Â   json_data = json.load(f)

scene_count = len(json_data)

â€‹

# Render README

readme = render_readme(title, scene_count)

readme_path = DATA / "readme.txt"

readme_path.write_text(readme)

â€‹

# Create ZIP

zip_path = ROOT / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.zip"

with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:

 Â   for file in track(DATA.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):

 Â  Â  Â   z.write(file, arcname=file.name)

â€‹

console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} with {scene_count} scenes![/]")


@app.command()
def build(title: str = typer.Argument(..., help="Song or project title")):
    """
    Build a complete storyboard ZIP package.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    package_storyboard(title)
@app.command()
def open_folder():
    """Open the storyboard project folder."""
    subprocess.run(["open", str(ROOT)])
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()

ğŸ§© File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py (Enhanced)
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI (Enhanced)
Creates, manages, and packages cinematic lyric storyboards.
All saves and builds are stored in /projects/{bname}.
"""
import json, pathlib, zipfile, csv, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track
app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()
ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
PROJECTS = ROOT / "projects"
TEMPLATE = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"
PROJECTS.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    template = Template(TEMPLATE.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)
def get_project_path(bname: str) -> pathlib.Path:
    path = PROJECTS / bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    path.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    return path
@app.command()
def generate(bname: str):
    """
    Generate a new storyboard template for a project.
    Example:
        storyboard generate Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    console.print(f"[cyan]Creating new storyboard template in {p}[/]")




 



# Create blank CSV

csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"

csv_headers = [

 Â   "scene_id","timestamp","scene_type","lyric_line","mood",

 Â   "lighting_style","camera_style","color_palette","symbolism",

 Â   "prompt_description","transition_method"

]

with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as f:

 Â   writer = csv.writer(f)

 Â   writer.writerow(csv_headers)

â€‹

# Create blank JSON

json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"

json_path.write_text("[]")

â€‹

# Create blank text file

txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"

txt_path.write_text(f"{bname} â€” Cinematic Storyboard\n\n[Add scenes here]\n")

â€‹

console.print("[green]âœ… Blank storyboard files created![/]")


@app.command()
def build(bname: str):
    """
    Build a storyboard ZIP package from /projects/{bname}.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")




 



json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"

csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"

txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"

â€‹

if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():

 Â   console.print("[red]Missing storyboard files in project folder![/]")

 Â   raise typer.Exit(1)

â€‹

json_data = json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]")

scene_count = len(json_data)

â€‹

# Render README

readme = render_readme(bname, scene_count)

(p / "readme.txt").write_text(readme)

â€‹

# Build ZIP

zip_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.zip"

console.print(f"[cyan]Packaging {bname}...[/]")

with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:

 Â   for file in track(p.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):

 Â  Â  Â   if file.is_file() and not file.name.endswith(".zip"):

 Â  Â  Â  Â  Â   z.write(file, arcname=file.name)

console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} in {p}[/]")


@app.command()
def list_projects():
    """List all available storyboard projects."""
    console.print("[bold yellow]Available Projects:[/]")
    for proj in PROJECTS.iterdir():
        if proj.is_dir():
            console.print(f" - {proj.name}")
@app.command()
def open_project(bname: str):
    """Open a storyboard project folder in Finder."""
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    subprocess.run(["open", str(p)])
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()
ğŸ’¡ Usage Examples
Command	Description
storyboard generate Stormchild	Creates new /projects/stormchild/ with blank CSV, JSON, TXT.
storyboard build Stormchild	Packages files in /projects/stormchild/ into stormchild_storyboard.zip.
storyboard list-projects	Shows all storyboards under /projects/.
storyboard open-project Stormchild	Opens the Stormchild folder in Finder.
âœ… Project Folder Layout (auto-generated)
projects/
 â””â”€ stormchild/
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
     â”œâ”€ readme.txt
     â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip

     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv

Got it âš¡ â€” letâ€™s lock in your **comprehensive DiGiTaL DiVe image generation workflow** and refine the transitions so theyâ€™re not just narratively strong but also visually coherent when sequenced in Runway, DALLÂ·E, or Sora.

---

# ğŸ¬ **DiGiTaL DiVe Narrative Image Generation Framework**

## 1. **Cover Image (Scene Introduction)**

* **Purpose:** Establish tone, mood, and symbolic entry point.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Wide vertical 9:16 frame. A symbolic object or environment (e.g., glowing graffiti heart, broken throne, willow tree through asphalt). High-contrast lighting (neon vs dark). Typography organically embedded (graffiti, billboard, sign).*
* **Transitions:** Begin with **slow aerial pan** or **fade-in from darkness**.

---

## 2. **Transition (Shift / Detail)**

* **Purpose:** Bridge focus from macro to micro or shift mood.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Close-up of symbolic lyric object (e.g., cracked cassette, dripping neon tear, barbed willow branch). Background blurred, softer lighting. Optional ghostly text integrated in mist, reflection, or scratched surface.*
* **Transitions:** Use **slow zoom-in/out** or **blur-to-clear reveal**.

---

## 3. **Main Image (Core Action / Emotion)**

* **Purpose:** Showcase the central action or emotional highlight.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Dynamic vertical 9:16 scene. Character(s) in motion (singing, rebelling, breaking down). Dramatic neon lighting palette (deep blues, pinks, reds). Typography as glowing signage or wall graffiti (chorus lyric). Action foregrounded, environment contextual.*
* **Transitions:** **Tracking shot or dolly sweep**, carry movement across cuts.

---

## 4. **Filler (Pause / Reflection)**

* **Purpose:** Add atmosphere, give narrative breathing room.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Static or slow tilt. Symbolic element (discarded item, rising smoke, graffiti wall). Warm or nostalgic lighting (golden, soft shadows). Typography faint or etched subtly (â€œhope never diesâ€).*
* **Transitions:** **Slow fade into dawn light**, or **subtle upward camera tilt**.

---

## 5. **Next-Scene Transition**

* **Purpose:** Expand scope or shift location for next narrative beat.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Panoramic 16:9 or wide vertical 9:16 view. Wider environment revealed (alley to skyline, ruins to protest). Colors fade or shift (pastel dawn, muted blues). Typography optional as lingering echo.*
* **Transitions:** **Whip-pan**, **glitch flicker**, or **crane pull-out**.

---

# âš™ï¸ **Technical Defaults**

* **Aspect Ratios:**

  * Characters â†’ 9:16 (1080x1920)
  * Cityscapes / Wide views â†’ 16:9 (1280x720)
  * Symbols / Objects â†’ 1:1 (1024x1024)
* **Typography:** Embedded naturally in-world, never overlaid.
* **Backgrounds:** Isolated + solid color for symbolic object focus.
* **Lighting:** Consistently cinematic, neon-vs-dark contrasts, transitions softened.

---

# ğŸ”„ **Batching Workflow**

* Always **generate 4 images per batch**:

  * 1 Ã— Cover or Main
  * 1 Ã— Transition
  * 1 Ã— Filler
  * 1 Ã— Next-Scene (or additional Main)
* After each batch: propose **4 new lyric-rooted expansions**:

  1. Expand on metaphor
  2. Explore secondary symbol
  3. Add emotional shift
  4. Alternate perspective

---

ChatGPT said:

Great â€” hereâ€™s how you can set up a Mamba + conda-forge environment on macOS (Intel) so that you can generate and manage storyboards like stormchild_storyboard.zip locally.
This will let you script CSV/JSON creation, run export automations, and later connect to image-generation or Sora workflows.

ğŸ§° Step 1. Install Miniforge (conda-forge native)

Miniforge is the lightweight conda distribution that defaults to the conda-forge channel.

# Download Miniforge for macOS Intel
curl -L -O https://github.com/conda-forge/miniforge/releases/latest/download/Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh

# Run the installer
bash Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh


Then restart your shell so conda works.

ğŸ Step 2. Install Mamba

Mamba is a fast drop-in replacement for conda.

conda install mamba -n base -c conda-forge


Check it works:

mamba --version

ğŸ§© Step 3. Create a dedicated environment

Letâ€™s make an environment for storyboard generation and export scripting:

mamba create -n storyboard python=3.11 pandas numpy rich jinja2 typer
mamba activate storyboard


These packages give you:

pandas â€“ CSV/JSON handling

numpy â€“ quick array math

rich â€“ styled console output

jinja2 â€“ templating (for readme generation)

typer â€“ command-line interface scripting

ğŸ–‹ï¸ Step 4. Add your StoryBoarder project structure

Inside your working folder:

stormchild_project/
 â”œâ”€ data/
 â”‚   â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
 â”‚   â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
 â”‚   â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
 â”œâ”€ scripts/
 â”‚   â””â”€ package_storyboard.py
 â””â”€ readme_template.j2

ğŸ§  Step 5. Example packaging script

Save this as scripts/package_storyboard.py:

import csv, json, shutil, zipfile, pathlib
from rich.console import Console
from jinja2 import Template

console = Console()
root = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
data = root / "data"
readme_template = root / "readme_template.j2"

def package_storyboard():
    console.print("[bold cyan]Packaging Stormchild storyboard...[/]")
    with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.csv") as f:
        csv_data = f.read()
    with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.json") as f:
        json_data = json.load(f)
    readme_text = Template(readme_template.read_text()).render(
        scenes=len(json_data), title="Stormchild"
    )

    (data / "readme.txt").write_text(readme_text)
    zip_path = root / "stormchild_storyboard.zip"
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as z:
        for file in data.iterdir():
            z.write(file, arcname=file.name)
    console.print(f"[green]Created {zip_path.name} successfully![/]")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    package_storyboard()


Run it:

python scripts/package_storyboard.py


Youâ€™ll get stormchild_storyboard.zip in the project root.

ğŸ§± Step 6. Reuse for other songs

To build future storyboards, just drop new CSV/JSON/text sets into data/, adjust the template, and rerun the script.

Would you like me to also add an optional command-line tool (typer-based CLI) so you can generate or repackage any storyboard project just by typing storyboard build stormchild?

You said:

ChatGPT said:

Perfect ğŸ¬ â€” hereâ€™s your next step: a Typer-based CLI tool that turns your storyboard packaging workflow into a simple command you can run from anywhere.

ğŸ§° File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI
----------------
Command-line interface for generating, packaging, and exporting cinematic
storyboards (CSV + JSON + text) into a zipped deliverable.
"""

import json, pathlib, zipfile, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track

app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()

ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
DATA = ROOT / "data"
TEMPLATES = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"


def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    """Render the README file from the Jinja2 template."""
    template = Template(TEMPLATES.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)


def package_storyboard(title: str):
    """Zip all storyboard files and a generated README into one archive."""
    console.print(f"[bold cyan]Building storyboard package for {title}...[/]")

    # Ensure data folder exists
    if not DATA.exists():
        console.print("[red]Data folder not found![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    # Load JSON data to count scenes
    json_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.json"
    csv_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.csv"
    txt_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.txt"

    if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():
        console.print("[red]Missing storyboard data files![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    with open(json_path) as f:
        json_data = json.load(f)
    scene_count = len(json_data)

    # Render README
    readme = render_readme(title, scene_count)
    readme_path = DATA / "readme.txt"
    readme_path.write_text(readme)

    # Create ZIP
    zip_path = ROOT / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.zip"
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
        for file in track(DATA.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):
            z.write(file, arcname=file.name)

    console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} with {scene_count} scenes![/]")


@app.command()
def build(title: str = typer.Argument(..., help="Song or project title")):
    """
    Build a complete storyboard ZIP package.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    package_storyboard(title)


@app.command()
def open_folder():
    """Open the storyboard project folder."""
    subprocess.run(["open", str(ROOT)])


if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()

âš™ï¸ Installation

Make it executable and add it to your PATH:

chmod +x scripts/storyboard_cli.py
echo 'alias storyboard="python /path/to/your/project/scripts/storyboard_cli.py"' >> ~/.zshrc
source ~/.zshrc

ğŸ§© File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py (Enhanced)
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI (Enhanced)
---------------------------
Creates, manages, and packages cinematic lyric storyboards.
All saves and builds are stored in /projects/{bname}.
"""

import json, pathlib, zipfile, csv, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track

app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()

ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
PROJECTS = ROOT / "projects"
TEMPLATE = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"
PROJECTS.mkdir(exist_ok=True)


def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    template = Template(TEMPLATE.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)


def get_project_path(bname: str) -> pathlib.Path:
    path = PROJECTS / bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    path.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    return path


@app.command()
def generate(bname: str):
    """
    Generate a new storyboard template for a project.
    Example:
        storyboard generate Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    console.print(f"[cyan]Creating new storyboard template in {p}[/]")

    # Create blank CSV
    csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"
    csv_headers = [
        "scene_id","timestamp","scene_type","lyric_line","mood",
        "lighting_style","camera_style","color_palette","symbolism",
        "prompt_description","transition_method"
    ]
    with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as f:
        writer = csv.writer(f)
        writer.writerow(csv_headers)

    # Create blank JSON
    json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"
    json_path.write_text("[]")

    # Create blank text file
    txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"
    txt_path.write_text(f"{bname} â€” Cinematic Storyboard\n\n[Add scenes here]\n")

    console.print("[green]âœ… Blank storyboard files created![/]")


@app.command()
def build(bname: str):
    """
    Build a storyboard ZIP package from /projects/{bname}.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")

    json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"
    csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"
    txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"

    if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():
        console.print("[red]Missing storyboard files in project folder![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    json_data = json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]")
    scene_count = len(json_data)

    # Render README
    readme = render_readme(bname, scene_count)
    (p / "readme.txt").write_text(readme)

    # Build ZIP
    zip_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.zip"
    console.print(f"[cyan]Packaging {bname}...[/]")
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
        for file in track(p.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):
            if file.is_file() and not file.name.endswith(".zip"):
                z.write(file, arcname=file.name)
    console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} in {p}[/]")


@app.command()
def list_projects():
    """List all available storyboard projects."""
    console.print("[bold yellow]Available Projects:[/]")
    for proj in PROJECTS.iterdir():
        if proj.is_dir():
            console.print(f" - {proj.name}")


@app.command()
def open_project(bname: str):
    """Open a storyboard project folder in Finder."""
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    subprocess.run(["open", str(p)])


if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()

ğŸ’¡ Usage Examples
Command	Description
storyboard generate Stormchild	Creates new /projects/stormchild/ with blank CSV, JSON, TXT.
storyboard build Stormchild	Packages files in /projects/stormchild/ into stormchild_storyboard.zip.
storyboard list-projects	Shows all storyboards under /projects/.
storyboard open-project Stormchild	Opens the Stormchild folder in Finder.

     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
     â”œâ”€ readme.txt
     â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip


Would you like me to add one more command â€” storyboard render stormchild â€” that automatically merges the CSV/JSON and outputs a single formatted cinematic storyboard text file (like the one I generated earlier)?

the stormchild is the name of the song
ChatGPT said:

Exactly right ğŸŒ©ï¸ â€” in this setup, â€œStormchildâ€ is the song title and therefore also the project name (bname) used by the CLI.

That means all of your song-specific outputs will live under a folder named after that title:

projects/
 â””â”€ stormchild/
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
     â”œâ”€ readme.txt
     â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip


So when you run:

it creates this structure, and then

packages everything in that folder into a ready-to-share zip file.

A symbolic object or environment (e.g., glowing graffiti heart, broken throne, willow tree through asphalt). High-contrast lighting (neon vs dark). Typography organically embedded (graffiti, billboard, sign).* * **Transitions:** Begin with **slow aerial pan** or **fade-in from darkness**. --- ## 2. **Transition (Shift / Detail)** * **Purpose:** Bridge focus from macro to micro or shift mood. * **Prompt Template:** *Close-up of symbolic lyric object (e.g., cracked cassette, dripping neon tear, barbed willow branch). Background blurred, softer lighting. Optional ghostly text integrated in mist, reflection, or scratched surface.* * **Transitions:** Use **slow zoom-in/out** or **blur-to-clear reveal**. --- ## 3. **Main Image (Core Action / Emotion)** * **Purpose:** Showcase the central action or emotional highlight. * **Prompt Template:** *Dynamic vertical 9:16 scene. Character(s) in motion (singing, rebelling, breaking down). Dramatic neon lighting palette (deep blues, pinks, reds). Typography as glowing signage or wall graffiti (chorus lyric). Action foregrounded, environment contextual.* * **Transitions:** **Tracking shot or dolly sweep**, carry movement across cuts. --- ## 4. **Filler (Pause / Reflection)** * **Purpose:** Add atmosphere, give narrative breathing room. * **Prompt Template:** *Static or slow tilt. Symbolic element (discarded item, rising smoke, graffiti wall). Warm or nostalgic lighting (golden, soft shadows). Typography faint or etched subtly (â€œhope never diesâ€).* * **Transitions:** **Slow fade into dawn light**, or **subtle upward camera tilt**. --- ## 5. **Next-Scene Transition** * **Purpose:** Expand scope or shift location for next narrative beat. * **Prompt Template:** *Panoramic 16:9 or wide vertical 9:16 view. Wider environment revealed (alley to skyline, ruins to protest). Colors fade or shift (pastel dawn, muted blues). You said: yes.. also lets setup a mamba conda-forge setup for macos intel to create ChatGPT said: Great â€” hereâ€™s how you can set up a Mamba + conda-forge environment on macOS (Intel) so that you can generate and manage storyboards like stormchild_storyboard.zip locally. This will let you script CSV/JSON creation, run export automations, and later connect to image-generation or Sora workflows. ğŸ§° Step 1. Install Miniforge (conda-forge native) Miniforge is the lightweight conda distribution that defaults to the conda-forge channel. # Download Miniforge for macOS Intel curl -L -O https://github.com/conda-forge/miniforge/releases/latest/download/Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh # Run the installer bash Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh Then restart your shell so conda works. ğŸ Step 2. Install Mamba Mamba is a fast drop-in replacement for conda. conda install mamba -n base -c conda-forge Check it works: mamba --version ğŸ§© Step 3. Create a dedicated environment Letâ€™s make an environment for storyboard generation and export scripting: mamba create -n storyboard python=3.11 pandas numpy rich jinja2 typer mamba activate storyboard These packages give you: pandas â€“ CSV/JSON handling numpy â€“ quick array math rich â€“ styled console output jinja2 â€“ templating (for readme generation) typer â€“ command-line interface scripting ğŸ–‹ï¸ Step 4. Add your StoryBoarder project structure Inside your working folder: stormchild_project/ â”œâ”€ data/ â”‚ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv â”‚ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json â”‚ â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt â”œâ”€ scripts/ â”‚ â””â”€ package_storyboard.py â””â”€ readme_template.j2 ğŸ§  Step 5. Example packaging script Save this as scripts/package_storyboard.py: import csv, json, shutil, zipfile, pathlib from rich.console import Console from jinja2 import Template console = Console() root = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1] data = root / "data" readme_template = root / "readme_template.j2" def package_storyboard(): console.print("[bold cyan]Packaging Stormchild storyboard...[/]") with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.csv") as f: csv_data = f.read() with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.json") as f: json_data = json.load(f) readme_text = Template(readme_template.read_text()).render( scenes=len(json_data), title="Stormchild" ) (data / "readme.txt").write_text(readme_text) zip_path = root / "stormchild_storyboard.zip" with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as z: for file in data.iterdir(): z.write(file, arcname=file.name) console.print(f"[green]Created {zip_path.name} successfully![/]") if __name__ == "__main__": package_storyboard() Run it: python scripts/package_storyboard.py Youâ€™ll get stormchild_storyboard.zip in the project root. ğŸ§± Step 6. Reuse for other songs To build future storyboards, just drop new CSV/JSON/text sets into data/, adjust the template, and rerun the script. âœ… Quick Summary Step Command Install Miniforge bash Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh Add Mamba conda install mamba -n base -c conda-forge Create env mamba create -n storyboard python=3.11 pandas numpy rich jinja2 typer Activate mamba activate storyboard Run packager python scripts/package_storyboard.py Would you like me to generate the readme_template.j2 Jinja template next, so it automatically formats the README file during packaging? You said: yes ChatGPT said: Perfect âš™ï¸ â€” hereâ€™s a ready-to-use readme_template.j2 for your Mamba/conda-forge storyboard packaging environment. Save this inside your project folder as: stormchild_project/readme_template.j2 ğŸ§© readme_template.j2 =========================================== ğŸ¬ {{ title }} â€” Cinematic Lyric Storyboard =========================================== Total Scenes: {{ scenes }} Runtime: 3:30 (210 seconds) Generated with: StoryBoarder (GPT-5 build) ------------------------------------------- ğŸ“˜ Project Overview ------------------------------------------- {{ title }} transforms lyrical text into a cinematic visual narrative. Each scene blends descriptive storytelling, emotional tone, and detailed visual direction â€” optimized for Runway, Sora, or DALLÂ·E sequence generation. Use the timestamps to sync visual moments with the audio. ------------------------------------------- ğŸ“ Files Included ------------------------------------------- 1. {{ title|lower }}_storyboard.txt â†’ Full cinematic narrative storyboard (rich descriptive text) 2. {{ title|lower }}_storyboard.csv â†’ Structured metadata table for each scene - scene_id, timestamp, lyric_line - mood, lighting, camera, symbolism, description, transition 3. {{ title|lower }}_storyboard.json â†’ Same data in JSON format for integration into pipelines 4. readme.txt (this file) â†’ Automatically generated from readme_template.j2 ------------------------------------------- ğŸ¨ Technical Notes ------------------------------------------- â€¢ Default Aspect Ratios: - Character/portrait: 9:16 (1080x1920) - Landscape/wide: 16:9 (1280x720) - Symbolic/object: 1:1 (1024x1024) â€¢ Lighting Palette: Warm candlelight, amber dawns, gentle blue storms, silver reflections, and gold twilight tones. â€¢ Sound Cues: Rain hum, wind through birch, lullaby echoes, laughter, and the breath of dawn. ------------------------------------------- ğŸ§© Usage ------------------------------------------- 1ï¸âƒ£ Edit or expand your CSV and JSON scenes under /data. 2ï¸âƒ£ Run: python scripts/package_storyboard.py 3ï¸âƒ£ The script will render this README and compress all data files into a final ZIP: {{ title|lower }}_storyboard.zip ------------------------------------------- ğŸ’¡ Credits ------------------------------------------- Storyboard generation, scene composition, and metadata design: â†’ StoryBoarder (GPT-5 cinematic lyric visualizer) Framework: DiGiTaL DiVe Narrative Workflow Audio Inspiration: "Stormchild" by Steven (Suno Project) ------------------------------------------- When you run your packaging script, this template will automatically generate a customized README with the song title and total scene count (calculated from your JSON file). Would you like me to also add an optional command-line tool (typer-based CLI) so you can generate or repackage any storyboard project just by typing storyboard build stormchild? You said: yes ChatGPT said: Perfect ğŸ¬ â€” hereâ€™s your next step: a Typer-based CLI tool that turns your storyboard packaging workflow into a simple command you can run from anywhere. ğŸ§° File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py #!/usr/bin/env python3 """ StoryBoarder CLI ---------------- Command-line interface for generating, packaging, and exporting cinematic storyboards (CSV + JSON + text) into a zipped deliverable. """ import json, pathlib, zipfile, subprocess import typer from jinja2 import Template from rich.console import Console from rich.progress import track app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False) console = Console() ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1] DATA = ROOT / "data" TEMPLATES = ROOT / "readme_template.j2" def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int): """Render the README file from the Jinja2 template.""" template = Template(TEMPLATES.read_text()) return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count) def package_storyboard(title: str): """Zip all storyboard files and a generated README into one archive.""" console.print(f"[bold cyan]Building storyboard package for {title}...[/]") # Ensure data folder exists if not DATA.exists(): console.print("[red]Data folder not found![/]") raise typer.Exit(1) # Load JSON data to count scenes json_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.json" csv_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.csv" txt_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.txt" if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists(): console.print("[red]Missing storyboard data files![/]") raise typer.Exit(1) with open(json_path) as f: json_data = json.load(f) scene_count = len(json_data) # Render README readme = render_readme(title, scene_count) readme_path = DATA / "readme.txt" readme_path.write_text(readme) # Create ZIP zip_path = ROOT / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.zip" with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z: for file in track(DATA.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."): z.write(file, arcname=file.name) console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} with {scene_count} scenes![/]") @app.command() def build(title: str = typer.Argument(..., help="Song or project title")): """ Build a complete storyboard ZIP package. Example: storyboard build Stormchild """ package_storyboard(title) @app.command() def open_folder(): """Open the storyboard project folder.""" subprocess.run(["open", str(ROOT)]) if __name__ == "__main__": app() âš™ï¸ Installation Make it executable and add it to your PATH: chmod +x scripts/storyboard_cli.py echo 'alias storyboard="python /path/to/your/project/scripts/storyboard_cli.py"' >> ~/.zshrc source ~/.zshrc ğŸ’¡ Usage Command Description storyboard build Stormchild Builds the Stormchild zip package. storyboard open-folder Opens the current storyboard directory in Finder. Youâ€™ll get a colorized progress bar from rich, automatic scene counting, and a complete zip containing: stormchild_storyboard.txt stormchild_storyboard.csv stormchild_storyboard.json readme.txt Would you like me to extend this CLI with a â€œgenerate-templateâ€ command that can auto-create new empty storyboards (folders + blank CSV/JSON) for future songs? You said: yes. HOWEVER the saves are based on each bname ChatGPT said: Excellent refinement âš™ï¸ â€” you want each new storyboard project to be auto-named and saved by its project name (bname), e.g.: projects/ â”œâ”€ stormchild/ â”‚ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt â”‚ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv â”‚ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json â”‚ â”œâ”€ readme.txt â”‚ â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip â”œâ”€ another_song/ â”‚ â”œâ”€ another_song_storyboard.txt â”‚ ... All saves and builds are stored in /projects/{bname}. """ import json, pathlib, zipfile, csv, subprocess import typer from jinja2 import Template from rich.console import Console from rich.progress import track app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False) console = Console() ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1] PROJECTS = ROOT / "projects" TEMPLATE = ROOT / "readme_template.j2" PROJECTS.mkdir(exist_ok=True) def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int): template = Template(TEMPLATE.read_text()) return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count) def get_project_path(bname: str) -> pathlib.Path: path = PROJECTS / bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") path.mkdir(exist_ok=True) return path @app.command() def generate(bname: str): """ Generate a new storyboard template for a project. Example: storyboard generate Stormchild """ p = get_project_path(bname) base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") console.print(f"[cyan]Creating new storyboard template in {p}[/]") # Create blank CSV csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv" csv_headers = [ "scene_id","timestamp","scene_type","lyric_line","mood", "lighting_style","camera_style","color_palette","symbolism", "prompt_description","transition_method" ] with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as f: writer = csv.writer(f) writer.writerow(csv_headers) # Create blank JSON json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json" json_path.write_text("[]") # Create blank text file txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt" txt_path.write_text(f"{bname} â€” Cinematic Storyboard\n\n[Add scenes here]\n") console.print("[green]âœ… Blank storyboard files created![/]") @app.command() def build(bname: str): """ Build a storyboard ZIP package from /projects/{bname}. Example: storyboard build Stormchild """ p = get_project_path(bname) base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json" csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv" txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt" if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists(): console.print("[red]Missing storyboard files in project folder![/]") raise typer.Exit(1) json_data = json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]") scene_count = len(json_data) # Render README readme = render_readme(bname, scene_count) (p / "readme.txt").write_text(readme) # Build ZIP zip_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.zip" console.print(f"[cyan]Packaging {bname}...[/]") with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z: for file in track(p.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."): if file.is_file() and not file.name.endswith(".zip"): z.write(file, arcname=file.name) console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} in {p}[/]") @app.command() def list_projects(): """List all available storyboard projects.""" console.print("[bold yellow]Available Projects:[/]") for proj in PROJECTS.iterdir(): if proj.is_dir(): console.print(f" - {proj.name}") @app.command() def open_project(bname: str): """Open a storyboard project folder in Finder.""" p = get_project_path(bname) subprocess.run(["open", str(p)]) if __name__ == "__main__": app() ğŸ’¡ Usage Examples Command Description storyboard generate Stormchild Creates new /projects/stormchild/ with blank CSV, JSON, TXT. storyboard build Stormchild Packages files in /projects/stormchild/ into stormchild_storyboard.zip. storyboard list-projects Shows all storyboards under /projects/. storyboard open-project Stormchild Opens the Stormchild folder in Finder. âœ… Project Folder Layout (auto-generated) projects/ â””â”€ stormchild/ â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt â”œâ”€ readme.txt â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip Would you like me to add one more command â€” storyboard render stormchild â€” that automatically merges the CSV/JSON and outputs a single formatted cinematic storyboard text file (like the one I generated earlier)? ## ğŸ¤– ChatGPT

#!/usr/bin/env python3 """ StoryBoarder CLI (Enhanced) --------------------------- Creates, renders, and packages cinematic lyric storyboards. All saves and builds live in /projects/{bname}. """ import csv, json, pathlib, zipfile, subprocess import typer from jinja2 import Template from rich.console import Console from rich.progress import track app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False) console = Console() ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1] PROJECTS = ROOT / "projects" TEMPLATE_README = ROOT / "readme_template.j2" TEMPLATE_STORY = ROOT / "storyboard_text_template.j2" PROJECTS.mkdir(exist_ok=True) def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int) -> str: tpl = Template(TEMPLATE_README.read_text()) return tpl.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count) def get_project_path(bname: str) -> pathlib.Path: p = PROJECTS / bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") p.mkdir(exist_ok=True) return p def load_data(project_dir: pathlib.Path, base: str): """Load CSV and JSON; JSON is canonical, CSV used for fallback/merge.""" json_path = project_dir / f"{base}_storyboard.json" csv_path = project_dir / f"{base}_storyboard.csv" data_json = [] if json_path.exists(): data_json = json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]") data_csv = {} if csv_path.exists(): with open(csv_path, newline="") as f: reader = csv.DictReader(f) for row in reader: try: sid = int(row.get("scene_id", "0") or "0") except ValueError: continue data_csv[sid] = row return data_json, data_csv def normalize_scene(scene: dict, csv_row: dict | None) -> dict: """Merge fields and provide safe defaults.""" s = dict(scene) if scene else {} sid = int(s.get("scene_id", csv_row.get("scene_id", 0))) if csv_row else int(s.get("scene_id", 0)) def pick(key, default=""): if s.get(key) not in (None, ""): return s[key] if csv_row and csv_row.get(key) not in (None, ""): return csv_row[key] return default return { "scene_id": sid, "timestamp": pick("timestamp"), "scene_type": pick("scene_type"), "lyric_line": pick("lyric_line"), "mood": pick("mood"), "lighting_style": pick("lighting_style"), "camera_style": pick("camera_style"), "color_palette": pick("color_palette"), "symbolism": pick("symbolism"), "prompt_description": pick("prompt_description"), "transition_method": pick("transition_method"), } @app.command() def generate(bname: str): """Scaffold an empty storyboard in /projects/{bname}.""" p = get_project_path(bname) base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") console.print(f"[cyan]Creating new storyboard template in {p}[/]") csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv" headers = [ "scene_id","timestamp","scene_type","lyric_line","mood", "lighting_style","camera_style","color_palette","symbolism", "prompt_description","transition_method" ] with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as f: csv.writer(f).writerow(headers) (p / f"{base}_storyboard.json").write_text("[]") (p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt").write_text(f"{bname} â€” Cinematic Storyboard\n\n[Add scenes here]\n") console.print("[green]âœ… Blank storyboard files created![/]") @app.command() def render(bname: str): """ Render a cinematic text storyboard from CSV/JSON using the Jinja template. Output: /projects/{bname}/{base}_storyboard.txt """ p = get_project_path(bname) base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") data_json, data_csv = load_data(p, base) if not data_json and not data_csv: console.print("[red]No storyboard data found. Add CSV/JSON first.[/]") raise typer.Exit(1) # Merge rows; prefer JSON, supplement with CSV. merged = [] # if JSON exists, use it as index, else build from CSV if data_json: for s in data_json: sid = int(s.get("scene_id", 0)) merged.append(normalize_scene(s, data_csv.get(sid))) else: for sid, r in data_csv.items(): merged.append(normalize_scene({}, r)) # Sort by scene_id, then timestamp as backup def sort_key(x): t = x.get("timestamp", "") return (int(x.get("scene_id", 0)), t) merged = sorted(merged, key=sort_key) # Render via template tpl = Template(TEMPLATE_STORY.read_text()) text = tpl.render(title=bname, scenes=merged) out_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt" out_path.write_text(text) console.print(f"[green]âœ… Rendered {out_path.name} with {len(merged)} scenes.[/]") @app.command() def build(bname: str): """Zip all files in /projects/{bname} into {base}_storyboard.zip.""" p = get_project_path(bname) base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_") json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json" csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv" if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists(): console.print("[red]Missing storyboard files in project folder![/]") raise typer.Exit(1) # Count scenes for README try: scenes = len(json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]")) except Exception: scenes = 0 readme = render_readme(bname, scenes) (p / "readme.txt").write_text(readme) zip_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.zip" console.print(f"[cyan]Packaging {bname}...[/]") with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z: for file in track(p.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."): if file.is_file() and file.name != zip_path.name: z.write(file, arcname=file.name) console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} in {p}[/]") @app.command() def list_projects(): """List all available storyboard projects.""" console.print("[bold yellow]Available Projects:[/]") for proj in PROJECTS.iterdir(): if proj.is_dir(): console.print(f" â€¢ {proj.name}") @app.command() def open_project(bname: str): """Open a storyboard project folder in Finder.""" p = get_project_path(bname) subprocess.run(["open", str(p)]) if __name__ == "__main__": app()

Got it âš¡ â€” letâ€™s lock in your **comprehensive DiGiTaL DiVe image generation workflow** and refine the transitions so theyâ€™re not just narratively strong but also visually coherent when sequenced in Runway, DALLÂ·E, or Sora.

---

# ğŸ¬ **DiGiTaL DiVe Narrative Image Generation Framework**

## 1. **Cover Image (Scene Introduction)**

* **Purpose:** Establish tone, mood, and symbolic entry point.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Wide vertical 9:16 frame. A symbolic object or environment (e.g., glowing graffiti heart, broken throne, willow tree through asphalt). High-contrast lighting (neon vs dark). Typography organically embedded (graffiti, billboard, sign).*
* **Transitions:** Begin with **slow aerial pan** or **fade-in from darkness**.

---

## 2. **Transition (Shift / Detail)**

* **Purpose:** Bridge focus from macro to micro or shift mood.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Close-up of symbolic lyric object (e.g., cracked cassette, dripping neon tear, barbed willow branch). Background blurred, softer lighting. Optional ghostly text integrated in mist, reflection, or scratched surface.*
* **Transitions:** Use **slow zoom-in/out** or **blur-to-clear reveal**.

---

## 3. **Main Image (Core Action / Emotion)**

* **Purpose:** Showcase the central action or emotional highlight.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Dynamic vertical 9:16 scene. Character(s) in motion (singing, rebelling, breaking down). Dramatic neon lighting palette (deep blues, pinks, reds). Typography as glowing signage or wall graffiti (chorus lyric). Action foregrounded, environment contextual.*
* **Transitions:** **Tracking shot or dolly sweep**, carry movement across cuts.

---

## 4. **Filler (Pause / Reflection)**

* **Purpose:** Add atmosphere, give narrative breathing room.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Static or slow tilt. Symbolic element (discarded item, rising smoke, graffiti wall). Warm or nostalgic lighting (golden, soft shadows). Typography faint or etched subtly (â€œhope never diesâ€).*
* **Transitions:** **Slow fade into dawn light**, or **subtle upward camera tilt**.

---

## 5. **Next-Scene Transition**

* **Purpose:** Expand scope or shift location for next narrative beat.
* **Prompt Template:**
  *Panoramic 16:9 or wide vertical 9:16 view. Wider environment revealed (alley to skyline, ruins to protest). Colors fade or shift (pastel dawn, muted blues). Typography optional as lingering echo.*
* **Transitions:** **Whip-pan**, **glitch flicker**, or **crane pull-out**.

---

# âš™ï¸ **Technical Defaults**

* **Aspect Ratios:**

  * Characters â†’ 9:16 (1080x1920)
  * Cityscapes / Wide views â†’ 16:9 (1280x720)
  * Symbols / Objects â†’ 1:1 (1024x1024)
* **Typography:** Embedded naturally in-world, never overlaid.
* **Backgrounds:** Isolated + solid color for symbolic object focus.
* **Lighting:** Consistently cinematic, neon-vs-dark contrasts, transitions softened.

---

# ğŸ”„ **Batching Workflow**

* Always **generate 4 images per batch**:

  * 1 Ã— Cover or Main
  * 1 Ã— Transition
  * 1 Ã— Filler
  * 1 Ã— Next-Scene (or additional Main)
* After each batch: propose **4 new lyric-rooted expansions**:

  1. Expand on metaphor
  2. Explore secondary symbol
  3. Add emotional shift
  4. Alternate perspective

---

# ğŸ“ **Example Batch (Optimized for Runway / Sora Motion)**

### **Image 1 â€“ Cover: â€œThe Neon Throneâ€**

* Prompt: *Wide vertical shot. A raccoon (symbolic frontman) slouched on a graffiti-covered dumpster throne beneath a flickering neon moon. Crown of soda tabs glints. Background: alley walls dripping with protest graffiti (â€œLoVe is RuBBishâ€).*
* Transition: **Fade-in from dark with neon flicker**.

---

### **Image 2 â€“ Transition: â€œBroken Reflectionsâ€**

* Prompt: *Close-up of a shattered bottle reflecting neon heart graffiti. Background: blurred brick wall with peeling concert posters. Droplets glow like pink tears. Ghostly lyric â€œRuBBish is Loveâ€ appears faintly in glass shards.*
* Transition: **Zoom into glass, dissolve into next scene**.

---

### **Image 3 â€“ Main: â€œDumpsterfire Chorusâ€**

* Prompt: *Dynamic shot. Character stands atop flaming dumpster stage, guitar in hand, crowd of urban creatures silhouetted. Neon and firelight clash in reds and blues. Graffiti chorus â€œLive Fast Eat Trashâ€ glows across the wall.*
* Transition: **Tracking dolly shot weaving through smoke**.

---

### **Image 4 â€“ Filler/Next: â€œAshes into Dawnâ€**

* Prompt: *Static low angle. Rising smoke clears, dawn light breaks over rooftops. Faded graffiti re-written: â€œHope Never Dies.â€ Leaves and ashes swirl upward in slow motion, glowing softly.*
* Transition: **Tilt upward, shift into pastel dawn**.

---

# â• **Four New Expansion Ideas**

1. A cracked mixtape glowing like a relic, projected against the alley wall.
2. Protest crowd carrying neon-lit instruments as banners.
3. Empty alley at night, lit only by graffiti that seems alive.
4. Moonlight spotlighting a lone rooftop figure whispering to the city.

Great â€” hereâ€™s how you can set up a Mamba + conda-forge environment on macOS (Intel) so that you can generate and manage storyboards like stormchild_storyboard.zip locally.
This will let you script CSV/JSON creation, run export automations, and later connect to image-generation or Sora workflows.

ğŸ§° Step 1. Install Miniforge (conda-forge native)

Miniforge is the lightweight conda distribution that defaults to the conda-forge channel.

# Download Miniforge for macOS Intel
curl -L -O https://github.com/conda-forge/miniforge/releases/latest/download/Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh

# Run the installer
bash Miniforge3-MacOSX-x86_64.sh


Then restart your shell so conda works.

ğŸ Step 2. Install Mamba

Mamba is a fast drop-in replacement for conda.

conda install mamba -n base -c conda-forge


Check it works:

mamba --version

ğŸ§© Step 3. Create a dedicated environment

Letâ€™s make an environment for storyboard generation and export scripting:

mamba create -n storyboard python=3.11 pandas numpy rich jinja2 typer
mamba activate storyboard


These packages give you:

pandas â€“ CSV/JSON handling

numpy â€“ quick array math

rich â€“ styled console output

jinja2 â€“ templating (for readme generation)

typer â€“ command-line interface scripting

ğŸ–‹ï¸ Step 4. Add your StoryBoarder project structure

Inside your working folder:

stormchild_project/
 â”œâ”€ data/
 â”‚   â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
 â”‚   â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
 â”‚   â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
 â”œâ”€ scripts/
 â”‚   â””â”€ package_storyboard.py
 â””â”€ readme_template.j2

ğŸ§  Step 5. Example packaging script

Save this as scripts/package_storyboard.py:

import csv, json, shutil, zipfile, pathlib
from rich.console import Console
from jinja2 import Template

console = Console()
root = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
data = root / "data"
readme_template = root / "readme_template.j2"

def package_storyboard():
    console.print("[bold cyan]Packaging Stormchild storyboard...[/]")
    with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.csv") as f:
        csv_data = f.read()
    with open(data / "stormchild_storyboard.json") as f:
        json_data = json.load(f)
    readme_text = Template(readme_template.read_text()).render(
        scenes=len(json_data), title="Stormchild"
    )

    (data / "readme.txt").write_text(readme_text)
    zip_path = root / "stormchild_storyboard.zip"
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w") as z:
        for file in data.iterdir():
            z.write(file, arcname=file.name)
    console.print(f"[green]Created {zip_path.name} successfully![/]")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    package_storyboard()


Run it:

python scripts/package_storyboard.py


Youâ€™ll get stormchild_storyboard.zip in the project root.

ğŸ§± Step 6. Reuse for other songs

To build future storyboards, just drop new CSV/JSON/text sets into data/, adjust the template, and rerun the script.

ChatGPT said:

Perfect ğŸ¬ â€” hereâ€™s your next step: a Typer-based CLI tool that turns your storyboard packaging workflow into a simple command you can run from anywhere.

ğŸ§° File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI
----------------
Command-line interface for generating, packaging, and exporting cinematic
storyboards (CSV + JSON + text) into a zipped deliverable.
"""

import json, pathlib, zipfile, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track

app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()

ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
DATA = ROOT / "data"
TEMPLATES = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"


def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    """Render the README file from the Jinja2 template."""
    template = Template(TEMPLATES.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)


def package_storyboard(title: str):
    """Zip all storyboard files and a generated README into one archive."""
    console.print(f"[bold cyan]Building storyboard package for {title}...[/]")

    # Ensure data folder exists
    if not DATA.exists():
        console.print("[red]Data folder not found![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    # Load JSON data to count scenes
    json_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.json"
    csv_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.csv"
    txt_path = DATA / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.txt"

    if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():
        console.print("[red]Missing storyboard data files![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    with open(json_path) as f:
        json_data = json.load(f)
    scene_count = len(json_data)

    # Render README
    readme = render_readme(title, scene_count)
    readme_path = DATA / "readme.txt"
    readme_path.write_text(readme)

    # Create ZIP
    zip_path = ROOT / f"{title.lower()}_storyboard.zip"
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
        for file in track(DATA.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):
            z.write(file, arcname=file.name)

    console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} with {scene_count} scenes![/]")


@app.command()
def build(title: str = typer.Argument(..., help="Song or project title")):
    """
    Build a complete storyboard ZIP package.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    package_storyboard(title)


@app.command()
def open_folder():
    """Open the storyboard project folder."""
    subprocess.run(["open", str(ROOT)])


if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()

âš™ï¸ Installation

Make it executable and add it to your PATH:

chmod +x scripts/storyboard_cli.py
echo 'alias storyboard="python /path/to/your/project/scripts/storyboard_cli.py"' >> ~/.zshrc
source ~/.zshrc

ğŸ’¡ Usage
Command	Description
storyboard build Stormchild	Builds the Stormchild zip package.
storyboard open-folder	Opens the current storyboard directory in Finder.

Youâ€™ll get a colorized progress bar from rich, automatic scene counting, and a complete zip containing:

stormchild_storyboard.txt
stormchild_storyboard.csv
stormchild_storyboard.json
readme.txt

 â”œâ”€ another_song/

 â”‚   ...


So weâ€™ll update the CLI to:

âœ… Automatically create a new folder under /projects/{bname}.
âœ… Save all files and the zip into that folder.
âœ… Allow storyboard generate {bname} to scaffold an empty storyboard (blank CSV, JSON, TXT).
âœ… Allow storyboard build {bname} to package any existing storyboard from that folder.

ğŸ§© File: scripts/storyboard_cli.py (Enhanced)
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
StoryBoarder CLI (Enhanced)
---------------------------
Creates, manages, and packages cinematic lyric storyboards.
All saves and builds are stored in /projects/{bname}.
"""

import json, pathlib, zipfile, csv, subprocess
import typer
from jinja2 import Template
from rich.console import Console
from rich.progress import track

app = typer.Typer(add_completion=False)
console = Console()

ROOT = pathlib.Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
PROJECTS = ROOT / "projects"
TEMPLATE = ROOT / "readme_template.j2"
PROJECTS.mkdir(exist_ok=True)


def render_readme(title: str, scene_count: int):
    template = Template(TEMPLATE.read_text())
    return template.render(title=title, scenes=scene_count)


def get_project_path(bname: str) -> pathlib.Path:
    path = PROJECTS / bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    path.mkdir(exist_ok=True)
    return path


@app.command()
def generate(bname: str):
    """
    Generate a new storyboard template for a project.
    Example:
        storyboard generate Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")
    console.print(f"[cyan]Creating new storyboard template in {p}[/]")

    # Create blank CSV
    csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"
    csv_headers = [
        "scene_id","timestamp","scene_type","lyric_line","mood",
        "lighting_style","camera_style","color_palette","symbolism",
        "prompt_description","transition_method"
    ]
    with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as f:
        writer = csv.writer(f)
        writer.writerow(csv_headers)

    # Create blank JSON
    json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"
    json_path.write_text("[]")

    # Create blank text file
    txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"
    txt_path.write_text(f"{bname} â€” Cinematic Storyboard\n\n[Add scenes here]\n")

    console.print("[green]âœ… Blank storyboard files created![/]")


@app.command()
def build(bname: str):
    """
    Build a storyboard ZIP package from /projects/{bname}.
    Example:
        storyboard build Stormchild
    """
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    base = bname.lower().replace(" ", "_")

    json_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.json"
    csv_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.csv"
    txt_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.txt"

    if not json_path.exists() or not csv_path.exists():
        console.print("[red]Missing storyboard files in project folder![/]")
        raise typer.Exit(1)

    json_data = json.loads(json_path.read_text() or "[]")
    scene_count = len(json_data)

    # Render README
    readme = render_readme(bname, scene_count)
    (p / "readme.txt").write_text(readme)

    # Build ZIP
    zip_path = p / f"{base}_storyboard.zip"
    console.print(f"[cyan]Packaging {bname}...[/]")
    with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", compression=zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
        for file in track(p.iterdir(), description="Adding files..."):
            if file.is_file() and not file.name.endswith(".zip"):
                z.write(file, arcname=file.name)
    console.print(f"[green]âœ… Created {zip_path.name} in {p}[/]")


@app.command()
def list_projects():
    """List all available storyboard projects."""
    console.print("[bold yellow]Available Projects:[/]")
    for proj in PROJECTS.iterdir():
        if proj.is_dir():
            console.print(f" - {proj.name}")


@app.command()
def open_project(bname: str):
    """Open a storyboard project folder in Finder."""
    p = get_project_path(bname)
    subprocess.run(["open", str(p)])


if __name__ == "__main__":
    app()

ğŸ’¡ Usage Examples
Command	Description
storyboard generate Stormchild	Creates new /projects/stormchild/ with blank CSV, JSON, TXT.
storyboard build Stormchild	Packages files in /projects/stormchild/ into stormchild_storyboard.zip.
storyboard list-projects	Shows all storyboards under /projects/.
storyboard open-project Stormchild	Opens the Stormchild folder in Finder.
âœ… Project Folder Layout (auto-generated)
projects/
 â””â”€ stormchild/
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.json
     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.txt
     â”œâ”€ readme.txt
     â””â”€ stormchild_storyboard.zip

     â”œâ”€ stormchild_storyboard.csv
